<span id="freeTextContainer14120197285910873063">I got The Fourth Monkey by J D Barker book in Feb'17. And the best part about author and PR they never pushed us to finish the book. It took me more than 6 months to start the book and another month to finish it. The only reason behind slower speed was mobi version. Well, if you have watched Dexter or similar series, you will like the book Those reading this book the first time don't think it is a sequel. Actually, the author has started the story of a serial killer not from his first victim but</span>
  <span id="freeText14120197285910873063" style="display:none">I got The Fourth Monkey by J D Barker book in Feb'17. And the best part about author and PR they never pushed us to finish the book. It took me more than 6 months to start the book and another month to finish it. The only reason behind slower speed was mobi version. Well, if you have watched Dexter or similar series, you will like the book Those reading this book the first time don't think it is a sequel. Actually, the author has started the story of a serial killer not from his first victim but from sixth or seventh one.<br /><br />Porter is trying to solve the 4MK case for last 5 years in which 6 killings were already taken place. The killer was like Dexter, his main target would be a criminal who was cleaned in police records. Instead of killing criminal killer will kill female close relative (mainly daughter or sister) of the person. Before killing he would send warnings to criminals in a small box. The first warning would be the ear of girl which indicates "Hear No Evil". The second warning would be eye ball of girl which indicates 'See No Evil". The third warning would be the tongue of the victim which indicates 'Speak No Evil". By the time third warning box reaches criminal, the dead body would be found along with records of crimes done by the criminal. Killer had never left any clues unless he wanted police to know about something. But this time things were different. Warning box delivery guy met with an accident and ear in the box led to one of the richest and most powerful fellows of Chicago city. How would Porter solve the case? Along with box, Porter found diary left by 4MK. Well the book is in two parallels. Case which I mentioned above and incident of 4MK's teenage. <br /><br />The author claimed books rights for movie and series are sold before publishing the book. And I actually found book pace slow as series. 400+ pages long book can be filmed in 10-12 episodes easily. The language of the book is quite easy and straight. The author has covered areas of psychology and criminal science while writing the story. Well, I have read fewer books in this genre so I liked it.<br /><br />Detailed Review Link - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://chevusread.blogspot.in/2017/08/book-review-fourth-monkey-by-j-d-barker.html">http://chevusread.blogspot.in/2017/08...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14120197285910873063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2231586066" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2231586066" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2231586066?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2231586066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4532901638669887820">The long and short of this is: A serial killer has been terrorizing Chicago for over five years. The serial killer has become known as the Fourth Monkey (See No evil, Speak No evil - you get the picture). Then one night, his body is found. Police on the scene believe that he was on his way to deliver a message about a victim - who may very well be still alive. Detective Sam Porter has been the detective on the case. He has his own demons and many question if it is too soon for him to be diving i</span>
  <span id="freeText4532901638669887820" style="display:none">The long and short of this is: A serial killer has been terrorizing Chicago for over five years. The serial killer has become known as the Fourth Monkey (See No evil, Speak No evil - you get the picture). Then one night, his body is found. Police on the scene believe that he was on his way to deliver a message about a victim - who may very well be still alive. Detective Sam Porter has been the detective on the case. He has his own demons and many question if it is too soon for him to be diving into this investigation- but he does. He believes he can find the victim and unravel who the killer is and what haws motivated him over the years. Whew! What a ride!<br /><br />That is all I am going to say about the plot. What I will say is that I highly recommend this book if you enjoy clever, intelligent psychological thrillers! Of course, as you can tell from the blurb, this is not fairy tale. It is dark, gritty, suspenseful, mesmerizing and hard to put down. I loved that we got to see inside the mind of the killer. He gave us glimpses into his past which really sucked me in! I loved the ongoing investigations paired with the killer's past. I COULD NOT PUT THIS BOOK DOWN! (and neither should you!)<br /><br />Again, if you like gritty psychological thrillers (and can handle some gore) this book is for you! But be warned - this is hard to put down and may cause you to lose sleep!<br /><br />See more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.openbookpost.com">www.openbookpost.com</a></span>

<div id="review_1937286442" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1937286442" />
    <a title="Sue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3908840-sue"><img alt="Sue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298502446p2/3908840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1937286442?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue" href="/user/show/3908840-sue">Sue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/33154920-the-fourth-monkey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3908840-sue?shelf=catlady-booklover">catlady-booklover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3908840-sue?shelf=vip-reviewer">vip-reviewer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3908840-sue?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3908840-sue?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3908840-sue?shelf=serial-killer">serial-killer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3908840-sue?shelf=kindle-paperwhite">kindle-paperwhite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3908840-sue?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1937286442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8648555508299415333">THE FOUTH MONKEY (4MK) by talented author J.D. Barker is a dark and twisting novel; a combination of Se7en meets The Silence of the Lambs. Psychological thrillers are my favourite genre so was very much looking forward to reading it. As I started to read it, I was transported to a time when I watched my favourite movie, Se7en. I was drawn and hooked to this book, and had work not got in the way, I would have finished it earlier. <br/><br/>I would describe The Fourth Monkey as very graphic in parts and not</span>
  <span id="freeText8648555508299415333" style="display:none">THE FOUTH MONKEY (4MK) by talented author J.D. Barker is a dark and twisting novel; a combination of Se7en meets The Silence of the Lambs. Psychological thrillers are my favourite genre so was very much looking forward to reading it. As I started to read it, I was transported to a time when I watched my favourite movie, Se7en. I was drawn and hooked to this book, and had work not got in the way, I would have finished it earlier. <br /><br />I would describe The Fourth Monkey as very graphic in parts and not for the faint-hearted. The Four Monkey Killer (4MK) was a serial killer, who tortured his victims before killing them, mailing body parts back to their families.<br /><br />I enjoy reading books about serial killers in order to understand what makes them tick, getting inside the mind of a deranged and twisted character. Who is he? Why does he do this?<br /><br />The Four Monkeys comes from a shrine in Japan, where there is a carving above the entrance.<br />“HEAR NO EVIL, SEE NO EVIL, SPEAK NO EVIL. THE FOURTH MONKEY REPRESENTS, DO NO EVIL.” The serial killer follows this pattern.<br /> <br />The Four Monkey Killer (4MK) has terrorized the residents of Chicago, for over five years. There had been a massive manhunt for this serial killer. When his body is found, the police soon realize he was on his way to deliver one final message, one which proves he has taken another victim who may still be alive. <br /><br />Detective Sam Porter had been there from the beginning. As the lead investigator on the 4MK task force, Detective Sam Porter discovers a personal diary in the jacket pocket of the body, and Porter finds himself caught up in the mind of a psychopath. He must now try to save the life of a young girl…caught in the middle by this sadistic killer.<br /><br />“With only a handful of clues, the elusive killer’s identity remains a mystery. Time is running out and the Four Monkey Killer taunts from beyond the grave in this masterfully written fast-paced thriller.”<br /><br />The novel is told from multiple pints of view with the main two being Detective Sam Porter and from 4MK’s diary. This diary tells the story of his life from childhood to the evil monster he became. This diary is creepy and gave me the chills…but I had to know why!<br /><br />This is a very well written novel with engaging and flawed characters to add depth and tension to the story. An easy five stars for me. Preorder this novel. It will be worth your time!<br /><br />I predict that this novel is going to be one of the most talked about books of the year!<br /><br />I received an ARC copy of this novel. All opinions are my own and my review it unbiased.<br />Expected publication: June 27th 2017 by Houghton Mifflin Harcourt<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8648555508299415333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17646211909605729731">I enjoyed this story. The Four Monkey Killer "4MK" is one nasty piece of work. I love the books that get into the serial killers head, and this one was messed up! I think my favorite bits were the relationship between the detectives, and even the swat team. They had me busting out laughing! These are 3 characters that I'd love to read more about. Hint, hint. The only thing that kept this from being a five star book was the wording. Mostly it was fine, but occasionally some awkward dialogue would</span>
  <span id="freeText17646211909605729731" style="display:none">I enjoyed this story. The Four Monkey Killer "4MK" is one nasty piece of work. I love the books that get into the serial killers head, and this one was messed up! I think my favorite bits were the relationship between the detectives, and even the swat team. They had me busting out laughing! These are 3 characters that I'd love to read more about. Hint, hint. The only thing that kept this from being a five star book was the wording. Mostly it was fine, but occasionally some awkward dialogue would show up. It made the characters seem stiff. Still, I plan on sticking around with this author. He's good, and I think he can only get better. Yep, I'd recommend this book and author. Thanks much to Houghton Mifflin Harcourt, and Netgalley. <br />Update! August 5, 2019. The third part of this trilogy will be out in a few month's.<br />If you love mysteries, and "like me" love sniffing out the clues. . You're gonna love this! Since this book and numero dos, I've been hooked.</span>

<div id="review_2253856518" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2253856518" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394406877p2/2473504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2253856518?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/33154920-the-fourth-monkey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=own-ebook-kindle">own-ebook-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=adult-content">adult-content</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=detective-fiction">detective-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=own-audio-audible">own-audio-audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=listened-to-audiobook">listened-to-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=omg-cliffhanger">omg-cliffhanger</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2253856518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17939900113733588107"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“There is a fourth monkey, but nobody really knows about him,” I explained. Father nodded. “The first three monkeys define the rules we should all live by, but it’s the fourth that carries the most importance.” “Shizaru,” I said. “His name is Shizaru.” “He stands for do no evil,” Father said. “And that, of course, is the rub. Should someone see or hear evil, there is little one can do. When someone speaks evil, there is fault to be had, but when they do evil . . . well, when they do evil</blockquote></i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText17939900113733588107" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“There is a fourth monkey, but nobody really knows about him,” I explained. Father nodded. “The first three monkeys define the rules we should all live by, but it’s the fourth that carries the most importance.” “Shizaru,” I said. “His name is Shizaru.” “He stands for do no evil,” Father said. “And that, of course, is the rub. Should someone see or hear evil, there is little one can do. When someone speaks evil, there is fault to be had, but when they do evil . . . well, when they do evil there is no room for forgiveness.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b> Whoa... if you are guilty of a wrongdoing, lock up your loved ones because 4MK will be coming for one of them. He's a very busy boy punishing the impure, and he does so with purpose and a clear endgame in mind. He's intelligent, uncompromising, zealous, and he has a sh#t-load of baggage that helped shaped his behavior. Oh...you'll get to learn all about his past which was the most disturbing yet most engaging part (for me anyway). <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31125554.The_Fourth_Monkey__A_4MK_Thriller___1_" title="The Fourth Monkey (A 4MK Thriller, #1) by J.D. Barker" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fourth Monkey</a> could have been much darker than it was but I would still say it's not for the faint of heart. There's plenty of the grittiness and forced imagination that comes with serial killer novels so if you enjoy that type of read you likely won't be disappointed. <br /><br />I don't usually enjoy detective fiction, but a few credible and brutally honest goodreads friends five-starred this title and those stars are very rare. I figured if I were to read any detective fiction, this one would be the safest and I have to admit, I really enjoyed it. The author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8224327.J_D__Barker" title="J.D. Barker" rel="nofollow noopener">J.D. Barker</a> introduced some interesting and complex characters that allowed me to become effortlessly invested despite my hesitation. I will absolutely be continuing this series. After that cliffhanger, how can I not?<br /><br /><b>My favorite quote:</b><br /><i>"When someone is in trouble, they expect, they wait, for someone of authority to help them. I think it’s because that is how these things play out in the movies and on television. The hero always arrives at the last minute, foils the crime, and rescues those in distress from certain death as all other options are exhausted. The tears come after that, possibly a hug, followed by a commercial break before they wrap up the program. Real life doesn’t work that way. I’ve seen more lives end than I can count, and they all seem to hold that same expectation at the end, their eyes glancing at the door, waiting for their savior to arrive. He doesn’t, though. In real life, the only true savior is oneself."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17939900113733588107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1935876889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15751751216136161191">My book ish: <a href='https://heresthefuckingtwist.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> | <a href='https://instagram.com/thefuckingtwist/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Insta</a><br/><br/><b>Update - 2017.07.31</b><br/>I mean....bitch, please...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501533141ra/23467872.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was exactly what I needed this year. <b>Are you <i>effing kidding</i> me? It's SO GOOD.</b><br/><br/>Favourite movies: <i>Se7en</i> and <i>The Silence of the Lambs.</i> This book? A perfect lovechild of those two things but without being <i>too much</i> like those comparisons. You know what I mean?<br/><br/>It's new. It's different. But familiar and satisfying. <br/><br/>It's bloody and twisted and gory and clever and fun. <br/><br/>Serial killer fiction is a dime a dozen, so when something come</span>
  <span id="freeText15751751216136161191" style="display:none">My book ish: <a href="https://heresthefuckingtwist.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://instagram.com/thefuckingtwist/" rel="nofollow noopener">Insta</a><br><br><b>Update - 2017.07.31</b><br>I mean....bitch, please...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501533141ra/23467872.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was exactly what I needed this year. <b>Are you <i>effing kidding</i> me? It's SO GOOD.</b><br><br>Favourite movies: <i>Se7en</i> and <i>The Silence of the Lambs.</i> This book? A perfect lovechild of those two things but without being <i>too much</i> like those comparisons. You know what I mean?<br><br>It's new. It's different. But familiar and satisfying. <br><br>It's bloody and twisted and gory and clever and fun. <br><br>Serial killer fiction is a dime a dozen, so when something comes along that just <i>feels</i> good and different and gets your heart racing, you have to hand out 5 stars and praise the literary Gods for finally answering your book prayers.<br><br>Do you want to take a journey inside the mind of a depraved killer? Do you want to ride along with the determined detective who is hunting him? WHO DOESN'T!! Read this book. <br><br>The voices jump off the page. The scenes unfold in your mind's eye in so much detail it will have you cringing, wanting to look away but not being able to - like a bloody car crash. It's every dark and twisty thing you want it to be. The killer is clever and patient and knows what he's doing. This cop is damaged (not in an overwrought way) but smart, with a battery that doesn't quit, pushing the pacing of this book to the max.<br><br>Barker does characters and plotting so well. I love his voice and his style. He mixes the standard "serial killer mystery" with a level of horror writing that seriously had my jaw on the floor. I am so impressed, and definitely a new fan. <br><br>It took <i>forever</i> for this one to become available at the library, and it doesn't take a Detective Sam Porter to puzzle out why. I'm so glad I finally got around to reading this amazingness. <br><br>Put it in a needle and stick it straight in my veins - I'm fucking addicted.<br>___________________________<br>2017.07.27:<br>Review coming soon!<br><br>I leave for vacation tomorrow and I just don't have the time to say everything I want to say about this <b>gotdamn beast of a book!</b> So I'll just say this, until I can write more:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501187487ra/23427942.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15751751216136161191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2383663871?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luffy" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy">Luffy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/33154920-the-fourth-monkey">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2383663871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7424222377210152272">I must admit that this book is slightly derivative. There's only certain ways to write a gruesome story. But even if many authors are doing it, it's still a difficult job. Like Barcelona winning the treble.<br/><br/>Sam Porter is deliberately a common down-to-earth name. He is no Holmes or Poirot, but he has an eye for detail and a knack for connecting ideas. He also thrives under pressure. Sam is a working class hero in spirit.<br/><br/>The violent acts here are celebrated, and who can argue with the readership th</span>
  <span id="freeText7424222377210152272" style="display:none">I must admit that this book is slightly derivative. There's only certain ways to write a gruesome story. But even if many authors are doing it, it's still a difficult job. Like Barcelona winning the treble.<br /><br />Sam Porter is deliberately a common down-to-earth name. He is no Holmes or Poirot, but he has an eye for detail and a knack for connecting ideas. He also thrives under pressure. Sam is a working class hero in spirit.<br /><br />The violent acts here are celebrated, and who can argue with the readership that wants just that? To be amazed. These police cases that occur in fiction is a bit departing from the reality that we're aware of. But I raise a figurative glass to the author for having written a nail biting book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7424222377210152272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pkDyd1L52GLEztpUcNBovKgSpXp/a8TX7ylO8XnRVyqMAN19UygU26lEWRI4NQZr31Urdax/Uiz1fVBj2yB7ug==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Z+Abqvjmhu56Ny5KeDIOB5hJlzg7AB7c1IU7D9P3IlJNoDSg+TdKVxe9rQww12DQ7w4ZN+gUiCfO0SWdcQYOwg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Los señores del tiempo, una épica novela histórica ambientada en el medievo, se publica con gran éxito bajo un misterioso pseudónimo: Diego Veilaz.\n\nVictoria, 1192. Diago Vela, el legendario conde don Vela, retorna a su villa después de dos años en una peligrosa misión encomendada por el rey Sancho VI el Sabio de Navarra y encuentra a su hermano Nagorno desposado con la que era su prometida, la noble e intrigante Onneca de Maestu.\n\nUnai López de Ayala, Kraken, se enfrenta a unas desconcertantes muertes que siguen un modus operandi medieval. Son idénticas a los asesinatos descritos en la novela Los señores del tiempo: un envenenamiento con la «mosca española» ―la Viagra medieval―, unas víctimas emparedadas como se hacía antaño en el «voto de tinieblas» y un «encubamiento», que consistía en lanzar al río a un preso encerrado en un tonel junto con un gallo, un perro, un gato y una víbora.\n\nLas investigaciones llevarán a Kraken hasta el señor de la torre de Nograro, una casa-torre fortificada habitada ininterrumpidamente desde hace mil años por el primogénito varón. Pero el reverso de tanta nobleza es la tendencia de los señores de la torre a padecer el trastorno de identidad múltiple, un detalle que arrastrará a Estíbaliz a vivir una arriesgada historia de amor. \n\nUnai López de Ayala acabará descubriendo que Los señores del tiempo tiene mucho que ver con su propio pasado. Es la gran pregunta de este thriller diabólico, construido con la precisión de un reloj suizo.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8224327.J_D_Barker">About J.D. Barker</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8224327.J_D_Barker"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1400802396p3/8224327.jpg);'></div>

<a href="/author/show/8224327.J_D_Barker">J.D. Barker

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16437997697954740095">J.D. Barker is the New York Times and international best-selling author of numerous novels, including DRACUL and THE FOURTH MONKEY. His latest, SHE HAS A BROKEN THING WHERE HER HEART SHOULD BE, released March 31. He is currently collaborating with James Patterson. His books have been translated into two dozen languages, sold in more than 150 countries, and optioned for both film and television. Ba</span>
  <span id="freeText16437997697954740095" style="display:none">J.D. Barker is the New York Times and international best-selling author of numerous novels, including DRACUL and THE FOURTH MONKEY. His latest, SHE HAS A BROKEN THING WHERE HER HEART SHOULD BE, released March 31. He is currently collaborating with James Patterson. His books have been translated into two dozen languages, sold in more than 150 countries, and optioned for both film and television. Barker resides in coastal New Hampshire with his wife, Dayna, and their daughter, Ember.<br /><br />A note from J.D.<br />As a child I was always told the dark could not hurt me, that the shadows creeping in the corners of my room were nothing more than just that, shadows. The sounds nothing more than the settling of our old home, creaking as it found comfort in the earth only to move again when it became restless, if ever so slightly. I would never sleep without closing the closet door, oh no; the door had to be shut tight. The darkness lurking inside needed to be held at bay, the whispers silenced. Rest would only come after I checked under the bed at least twice and quickly wrapped myself in the safety of the sheets (which no monster could penetrate), pulling them tight over my head.<br /><br />I would never go down to the basement.<br /><br />Never.<br /><br />I had seen enough movies to know better, I had read enough stories to know what happens to little boys who wandered off into dark, dismal places alone. And there were stories, so many stories.<br /><br />Reading was my sanctuary, a place where I could disappear for hours at a time, lost in the pages of a good book. It didn’t take long before I felt the urge to create my own.<br /><br />I first began to write as a child, spinning tales of ghosts and gremlins, mystical places and people. For most of us, that’s where it begins—as children we have such wonderful imaginations, some of us have simply found it hard to grow up. I’ve spent countless hours trying to explain to friends and family why I enjoy it, why I would rather lock myself in a quiet little room and put pen to paper for hours at a time than throw around a baseball or simply watch television. Don’t get me wrong, sometimes I want to do just that, sometimes I wish for it, but even then the need to write is always there in the back of my mind, the characters are impatiently tapping their feet, waiting their turn, wanting to be heard. I wake in the middle of the night and reach for the pad beside my bed, sometimes scrawling page after page of their words, their lives. Then they’re quiet, if only for a little while. To stop would mean madness, or even worse—the calm, numbing sanity I see in others as they slip through the day without purpose. They don’t know what it’s like, they don’t understand. Something as simple as a pencil can open the door to a new world, can create life or experience death. Writing can take you to places you’ve never been, introduce you to people you’ve never met, take you back to when you first saw those shadows in your room, when you first heard the sounds mumbling ever so softly from your closet, and it can show you what uttered them. It can scare the hell out of you, and that’s when you know it’s good.<br /><br />jd</span>
  <a data-text-id="16437997697954740095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
